Prophethood
beginner
3 min
The Foundation of Divine Wisdom
Nasafi establishes God's wisdom and the consensus on that attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God's wisdom is a necessary attribute and that all His actions are wise, not foolish.

Core Idea
God's wisdom makes every divine act correct and purposeful.

Nasafi begins his proof of prophethood by establishing a foundational truth: God is perfectly wise, and nothing He does can be foolish. This premise is accepted by all who believe in a Creator. Understanding this is essential before we can evaluate the specific act of sending prophets.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once to get a feel for the language. Then read the translation.
Notice the terms 'حكمة' and 'سفه'.
2
Identify the key attributes
Focus on the attributes mentioned: God is حكيم (wise), and His actions are described as حكمة (wisdom) not سفه (foolishness), and are صواب (correct).
3
Reflect on the premise's role
Think about why this premise is placed at the start of a chapter on prophethood. It serves as the foundation for the next argument.
This is a typical kalam methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١- [الكلام (۱) في إثبات النبوة والرسالة]:
ثم إذا ثبت أن الله تعالى حكيم لا يخرج فعل من أفعاله عن الحكمة إلى السفه، ولا يخلو (۲) في شيء مما يأتي ويذر عن الوصف له بالإصابة. فبعد انعقاد الإجماع من القائلين بثبوت الصانع على هذه الجملة اختلفوا في أفعال متعينة. أن الله تعالى هل يجوز أن يفعلها، وهل هي في أنفسها حكمة أم هي " سفه فمن ذلك إرسال الله تعالى واحدًا قد اصطفاه من خليقته إلى عباده ليبين لهم ما يحتاجون إليه من مصالح الدارين. اختلفوا في جوازه (۳) وكونه حكمة فقال أئمة الهدى وقادة الخير وحكماء البشر : أنه حكمة وصواب، وقد أرسل الله تعالى إلى الخلق رسلا مبشرين ومنذرين. وأيدهم بالحجج والدلائل.
الذين يقولون لا حاجة للرسل]:
وقالت طوائف من الناس بامتناعه (٤) في نفسه، واختلفوا في علة الامتناع
1 – [Discussion on the Proof of Prophethood and Messengership]: Then, when it is established that God – exalted is He – is wise, not removing any of His actions from wisdom to foolishness, and is not free in anything He does or leaves from being described as correct. So after the consensus of those who affirm the existence of the Maker on this summary, they differed concerning specific actions: whether God – exalted is He – is permitted to do them, and whether they are in themselves wisdom or foolishness. Among that is God’s sending a chosen one from His creation to His servants to clarify for them what they need of the benefits of the two abodes. They differed concerning its permissibility and its being wisdom. So the Imams of guidance, leaders of good, and the wise of mankind said: it is wisdom and correctness, and God – exalted is He – has sent to creation messengers as bringers of good news and warners, and supported them with proofs and evidences. [Those who say there is no need for messengers]: And groups of people said it is impossible in itself, and they differed concerning the cause of impossibility.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on proving prophethood and messengership (إثبات النبوة والرسالة). It begins by establishing a foundational premise: God is wise (حكيم), and none of His actions fall outside wisdom into foolishness (سفه). Everything He does or omits is described as correct (إصابة). This premise is accepted by all who affirm the existence of the Creator. Despite this consensus on God's general wisdom, scholars disagreed about specific actions: whether God may perform them, and whether they are inherently wise or foolish. The specific action under discussion is sending a chosen messenger (رسول) from among creation to clarify what people need for their worldly and otherworldly welfare (مصالح الدارين). Some denied its permissibility or wisdom, but the Imams of guidance (أئمة الهدى), leaders of good (قادة الخير), and the wise among mankind (حكماء البشر) affirmed that sending messengers is wisdom and correctness (حكمة وصواب). They assert that God has indeed sent messengers as bringers of good news (مبشرين) and warners (منذرين), supporting them with proofs (حجج) and evidences (دلائل). The passage then transitions to the deniers, introduced under the heading 'Those who say there is no need for messengers' (الذين يقولون لا حاجة للرسل). These groups claim that prophethood is impossible in itself (امتناعه في نفسه) and differ on the cause of this impossibility. The author will presumably refute these positions in the following text.

Key Terms
حكمة (wisdom)
سفه (foolishness)
إصابة (correctness)
إجماع (consensus)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that God can act in foolish ways or that His actions are arbitrary.
Correction: The passage asserts that God's wisdom precludes any foolishness, and all His actions are correct.

Checkpoint
According to the premise, what describes all of God's actions?
A) Foolishness
B) Wisdom and correctness
C) Randomness
D) Necessity

Key Takeaway
God's wisdom is a necessary attribute, ensuring all His actions are wise and correct.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that every action of God in your life is correct and wise, how would your response to hardship change? What area of your life right now reveals a lack of trust in God's wisdom?
?
In what situation have you accused God of foolishness (maybe silently) by questioning His decree? Will you repent and affirm His absolute wisdom?
?
How does the certainty that God is never foolish affect your view of the Quran and the prophets? Will you submit to a command you don’t understand?

The Disagreement on Sending Messengers
Nasafi reports the differing views on whether sending messengers is wisdom and presents the Imams' affirmation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the central disagreement about prophethood: whether sending messengers is an act of wisdom or foolishness, and the position of the A'immah.

Core Idea
Sending prophets is a wise divine act, not foolishness.

After establishing God's wisdom, Nasafi turns to the specific act of sending messengers. He reports that some deny its permissibility or wisdom, while the Imams of guidance affirm it as wisdom and correctness. This lesson presents the debate and the orthodox position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the flow from consensus to disagreement to the two opposing views.
The passage includes a subheading about those who say there is no need for messengers.
2
Identify the two positions
What do the Imams say? What do the deniers say? Look for keywords: حكمة وصواب vs امتناع.
3
See the evidence provided
The Imams point to the historical fact that God sent messengers with proofs. This is presented as evidence for their view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١- [الكلام (۱) في إثبات النبوة والرسالة]:
ثم إذا ثبت أن الله تعالى حكيم لا يخرج فعل من أفعاله عن الحكمة إلى السفه، ولا يخلو (۲) في شيء مما يأتي ويذر عن الوصف له بالإصابة. فبعد انعقاد الإجماع من القائلين بثبوت الصانع على هذه الجملة اختلفوا في أفعال متعينة. أن الله تعالى هل يجوز أن يفعلها، وهل هي في أنفسها حكمة أم هي " سفه فمن ذلك إرسال الله تعالى واحدًا قد اصطفاه من خليقته إلى عباده ليبين لهم ما يحتاجون إليه من مصالح الدارين. اختلفوا في جوازه (۳) وكونه حكمة فقال أئمة الهدى وقادة الخير وحكماء البشر : أنه حكمة وصواب، وقد أرسل الله تعالى إلى الخلق رسلا مبشرين ومنذرين. وأيدهم بالحجج والدلائل.
الذين يقولون لا حاجة للرسل]:
وقالت طوائف من الناس بامتناعه (٤) في نفسه، واختلفوا في علة الامتناع
1 – [Discussion on the Proof of Prophethood and Messengership]: Then, when it is established that God – exalted is He – is wise, not removing any of His actions from wisdom to foolishness, and is not free in anything He does or leaves from being described as correct. So after the consensus of those who affirm the existence of the Maker on this summary, they differed concerning specific actions: whether God – exalted is He – is permitted to do them, and whether they are in themselves wisdom or foolishness. Among that is God’s sending a chosen one from His creation to His servants to clarify for them what they need of the benefits of the two abodes. They differed concerning its permissibility and its being wisdom. So the Imams of guidance, leaders of good, and the wise of mankind said: it is wisdom and correctness, and God – exalted is He – has sent to creation messengers as bringers of good news and warners, and supported them with proofs and evidences. [Those who say there is no need for messengers]: And groups of people said it is impossible in itself, and they differed concerning the cause of impossibility.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on proving prophethood and messengership (إثبات النبوة والرسالة). It begins by establishing a foundational premise: God is wise (حكيم), and none of His actions fall outside wisdom into foolishness (سفه). Everything He does or omits is described as correct (إصابة). The specific action under discussion is sending a chosen messenger (رسول) from among creation to clarify what people need for their worldly and otherworldly welfare (مصالح الدارين). Some denied its permissibility or wisdom, but the Imams of guidance (أئمة الهدى), leaders of good (قادة الخير), and the wise among mankind (حكماء البشر) affirmed that sending messengers is wisdom and correctness (حكمة وصواب). They assert that God has indeed sent messengers as bringers of good news (مبشرين) and warners (منذرين), supporting them with proofs (حجج) and evidences (دلائل). The passage then transitions to the deniers, introduced under the heading 'Those who say there is no need for messengers' (الذين يقولون لا حاجة للرسل). These groups claim that prophethood is impossible in itself (امتناعه في نفسه) and differ on the cause of this impossibility. The author will presumably refute these positions in the following text.

Key Terms
نبوة (prophethood)
رسالة (messengership)
حكمة (wisdom)
سفه (foolishness)
أئمة الهدى (Imams of guidance)
امتناع (impossibility)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that prophethood is impossible because it implies change in God or is unnecessary.
Correction: The Imams affirm it is wisdom and God actually sent messengers.

Checkpoint
What did the Imams of guidance say about God sending messengers?
A) It is impossible.
B) It is permissible but not wise.
C) It is wisdom and correctness.
D) It is foolishness.

Key Takeaway
The Imams of guidance affirm that sending messengers is a wise and correct act of God, contrary to those who claim its impossibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that God sending prophets was an act of perfect wisdom, even when His commands contradict your desires? How does your daily obedience reflect that belief?
?
If you were to defend the wisdom of prophethood to a skeptic, would your own life serve as evidence that following the messenger leads to wisdom? What needs to change?
?
Is there any area of your life where you act as if God's sending of messengers was foolish—by disregarding their teachings? Will you repent and align with His wisdom today?

The Naturalist Argument Against Miracles
The author presents the naturalist argument against miracles as proof of prophethood

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument of the naturalists who deny that miracles can prove prophethood, and why they conclude that sending a prophet would be futile.

Core Idea
Naturalists claim that miracles cannot prove prophethood because they are either imitable or impossible.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi presents the objection of the naturalist philosophers, a group that accepts God's existence but rejects the possibility of proving prophethood through miracles. They argue that any alleged miracle either falls within natural custom—and thus can be imitated by a false claimant—or falls outside it, which they deem impossible. This leads them to deny all reported miracles and to assert that divine sending of a prophet would be pointless without evidence. Understanding this objection is crucial before the author refutes it.

Guided Path
1
Read the naturalist argument
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully, noting the logical structure of their reasoning.
This is an objection being presented, not the author's own view.
2
Understand the dilemma
Identify the two options for a miracle (customary vs. extraordinary) and how each leads to failure of proof.
The naturalists think both options make miracles invalid as proof.
3
Consider the conclusion
Follow how the naturalists conclude that sending a prophet without proof would be futile, and that this is the view to be refuted.
The author will later refute this argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوقوف عليه حاجة. غير أن الامتناع جاء من ناحية أخرى، واختلف هؤلاء فيما بينهم، فمنهم من زعم أن الامتناع ثبت لما أن لا فائدة فيه إلا بعد ثبوته، ولا طريق للوصول إليه والوقوف على ثبوته، لما أن دعوى المتنبئ تعارض دعوى النبي. ولا يمكن الفصل بينهما إلا بالدليل ولا دليل على ذلك، لأن ما اقترن به من الدليل إما أن كان خارجًا على العادة المستمرة وعلى ما عليه أمور الطبائع، وإما أن كان خارجًا عن ذلك ; فإن كان خارجا على العادة الجارية والطبيعة الثابتة فلا يعجز المتنبئ عن الإتيان بمثله. وإن كان خارجا عن ذلك فهو محال إذ تغيير الطبائع وخروجها عما هي عليه أمر ممتنع والقول به محال وإلى هذا يذهب الطبيعيون وينكرون جميع ما ثبت بالتواتر من الأمور الخارجة عن المعتاد والأمر الطبيعي من نحو قلب العصا حية، وانفجار الماء من الصخر، وفلق البحر، وإبراء الأكمة والأبرص وإحياء الموتى، وكلام الناقة، والشاه المسمومة ونبع الماء من بين الأصابع وأشباه ذلك. وإذا كان الأمر كذلك فلو أرسل الله تعالى رسولاً، وليس في مقدوره إقامة الدليل على صدقه فلا فائدة فيه بدون ثبوت رسالته، ولا وجه إلى إثباته إذ لا إلى إقامة الدليل عليه، لكان ذلك الإرسال خاليًا عن العاقبة الحميدة متعريًا عن النفع والجدوى، وهو سفه والله تعالى يجل عن الوصف به.
It is necessary to pause upon it. However, the impossibility arose from another direction, and these people differed among themselves. Some of them claimed that impossibility is established because there is no benefit in it except after its establishment, and there is no way to reach it or to ascertain its establishment, because the claim of a false prophet contradicts the claim of a true prophet. And it is not possible to decide between them except by evidence, and there is no evidence for that, because the evidence associated with it is either outside the continuous custom and what is upon the natures of things, or outside that. If it is outside the prevailing custom and the fixed nature, then the false prophet is not incapable of coming with something similar. And if it is outside that, then it is impossible, because changing the natures and their departure from what they are is an impossible matter, and saying so is impossible. This is what the naturalists hold, and they deny all that has been established by tawatur (widespread transmission) of matters outside the customary and natural, such as the turning of the staff into a serpent, the gushing of water from rock, the splitting of the sea, the healing of the blind and the leprous, the reviving of the dead, the speaking of the she-camel, the poisoned sheep, the flowing of water from between the fingers, and the like. And if the matter is such, then if Allah Almighty sends a messenger, and it is not in his power to establish evidence for his truthfulness, then there is no benefit in it without the establishment of his messengership, and no way to prove it since there is no way to establish evidence for it. That sending would be devoid of praiseworthy consequence, stripped of benefit and usefulness, and that is foolishness, and Allah Almighty is exalted above being described with it.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage presents the objection of the first group of deniers of prophethood, those who accept the existence of God but deny the possibility of proving prophethood. The author begins by noting the necessity of pausing on this issue. He then explains that these deniers hold that proof of prophethood is impossible because there is no benefit in it unless established, and there is no way to establish it due to conflicting claims. They argue that the evidence accompanying a prophet's claim (a miracle) must be either within normal custom (natural) or outside it. If within custom, a false claimant can imitate it; if outside custom, it is impossible because changing nature is impossible—this is the position of the naturalists (al-tabi'iyyun). They consequently reject all reported miracles as unnatural and impossible. Therefore, if God were to send a messenger without providing evidence, it would be futile and senseless, which cannot be attributed to God. The author is reporting this view as part of a broader refutation.

Key Terms
الطبيعيون
التواتر
العادة
الطبيعة
المحال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The naturalists' argument is the author's own view.
Correction: The author is presenting this argument as an objection to be refuted later.

Checkpoint
According to the naturalists, why is it impossible for a prophet to provide a valid miracle as proof?
A) Because God does not perform miracles.
B) Because the miracle is either natural (imitable) or supernatural (impossible), and in both cases it cannot serve as proof.
C) Because prophets are not truthful.
D) Because miracles are only for followers of the law.

Key Takeaway
The naturalists' argument that miracles cannot prove prophethood hinges on a false dilemma: they assume miracles are either natural and imitable or supernatural and impossible, ignoring the possibility of divinely authenticated miracles that transcend nature and cannot be imitated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear an intellectually sophisticated argument that seems to disprove a core belief—like the naturalist argument against miracles—do you feel unsettled? Have you ever brushed it aside without honestly examining its assumptions? What would it take for you to engage such an argument with both critical thinking and faith?
?
The naturalists claim that changing nature is impossible. But if you truly believe God is All-Powerful, does your life reflect a readiness for the miraculous—or have you become so accustomed to natural patterns that you subconsciously limit what you expect from God?
?
The passage warns against a false dilemma: either a miracle is natural or impossible. Are there areas in your own faith where you have accepted a similar false choice (e.g., either science or religion, either reason or revelation)? Will you commit to rejecting such dichotomies and holding to the truth that God can work beyond both nature and human categories?

The Sorcerer's Miracles Objection
The author presents the second group's objection that sorcerers can also perform miracles, causing conflict.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second group's argument that sorcerers can also perform wonders, creating an undecidable conflict that undermines the proof of prophethood.

Core Idea
If sorcerers can also do miracles, then miracles prove nothing.

The author has already refuted one objection. Now he presents a second, more subtle one: even if we accept that God can perform miracles, sorcerers and magicians claim to do similar things. This creates a conflict with no way to tell the true prophet from the false, making the whole proof of prophethood collapse. Read carefully to see the full objection before we learn how it is answered.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Pay attention to the flow: the concession, the claim, the conflict, and the conclusion.
Notice that the objection starts by acknowledging God's power over nature.
2
Identify the two main claims
The passage makes two key claims: (1) God can cause extraordinary events, and (2) sorcerers can also do the same. This leads to the problem.
The first claim is a concession; the second is the real objection.
3
Understand the conflict (ta'āruḍ)
The term 'ta'āruḍ' means conflict or contradiction. Here it means that the miracles of the prophet and the feats of the sorcerer appear alike, so there is no way to prefer one over the other (lā tarjīḥ).
This is the core of the objection: no preponderance.
4
Trace the conclusion
The passage ends by recalling the earlier point: if there is no clear proof, sending a messenger is useless. This shows that the objection seeks to undermine the entire institution of prophethood.
The author will refute this later; here he is only reporting it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزعم بعض هؤلاء أن خروج الأمر عن المعتاد وقلب العادة والطبيعة في مقدور الله تعالى، إلا أن ذلك أيضا مقدور السحرة والمشعوذة فيقع بذلك تعارض بحيث لا ترجيح لأحد الأمرين على الآخر، وقد مر أن إرسال الرسول والحالة هذه خال عن العاقبة الحميدة متعريًا عن الجدوى.
And some of these claimed that the departure of matters from the customary and the overturning of custom and nature are within the power of Allah Almighty, except that that is also within the power of sorcerers and magicians, so by that a conflict occurs such that there is no preponderance of one of the two matters over the other. And it has already been stated that sending a messenger in such a state is devoid of praiseworthy consequence and stripped of usefulness.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage presents the objection of the second group of deniers. They concede that God has the power to cause extraordinary events (kharq al-‘ādah). However, they argue that sorcerers (al-saḥara) and magicians (al-musha‘widha) also have the power to perform similar feats. This leads to a conflict (ta‘āruḍ) between the miracle of the true prophet and the magic of the sorcerer, with no way to prefer one over the other (lā tarjīḥ). Since it was already established that sending a messenger without clear proof is futile, this situation likewise renders prophethood useless. The author is reporting this as another objection to be refuted.

Key Terms
السحرة
المشعوذة
التعارض
الترجيح
العادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think this objection is a valid defense of sorcery or a genuine philosophical difficulty.
Correction: The objection is a false claim that the author will refute; it is not an admission that sorcerers truly have divine powers or that miracles are indistinguishable from magic.

Checkpoint
What is the main problem the second group raises regarding miracles?
A) Miracles are impossible for God.
B) Sorcerers can also perform wonders, so there is no way to distinguish a true prophet from a false one.
C) Miracles are not beneficial.
D) Sorcerers are more powerful than prophets.

Key Takeaway
The second group argues that sorcerers can also perform wonders, creating an unresolvable conflict that would make miracles useless as proof of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were confronted with two equally impressive supernatural claims—one from a true prophet and one from a charlatan—what in your heart would actually distinguish them? Is your certainty in the prophethood of Muhammad ﷺ based on external wonders alone, or on something deeper? Own that foundation today.
?
When you hear of miraculous events in your community (e.g., dreams, healings), how do you instinctively respond? Do you evaluate them against the Quran and Sunnah, or do you accept them uncritically? This lesson warns that without distinction, messengers become useless—what does that imply about your own spiritual discernment?
?
The objection argues that if miracles are indistinguishable, then sending a messenger is pointless. Have you ever treated the Prophet's message as 'devoid of praiseworthy consequence' in your daily life? In what specific area have you failed to let his prophethood guide you? Commit now to renew your submission to his unique authority.

The Argument That Prophetic Evidence Can Be Imitated Through Practice
The author presents the third group's claim that prophetic signs can be acquired by others with training, hence no certainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third group's objection that prophetic miracles can be imitated by anyone with sufficient training, thus undermining the certainty of a prophet's truthfulness.

Core Idea
Miracles lose their evidential force if they can be replicated by anyone with enough training.

This passage presents a skeptical objection: if someone else could perform the same miraculous acts with enough effort and practice, then a prophet's miracle is not a unique sign from God. The author records this challenge to highlight why miracles alone may not suffice for certainty.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the literal translation to understand the objection in its own words.
Notice the key terms: تكلف, اجتهاد, تدرب, اعتياد.
2
Identify the core claim
The third group claims that the kind of evidence a prophet brings (miracles) can be acquired by anyone who puts in effort and practice.
They are not denying miracles, but their exclusivity.
3
Understand the reasoning
They argue that the prophet's audience may simply lack habituation in such acts, and the prophet did not test all humans. If he had, he might have found someone who could imitate him.
This reasoning is meant to introduce doubt.
4
Recognize the conclusion
Because of the possibility of falsehood (iḥtimāl al-buṭlān), no certain knowledge of the prophet's truthfulness can be attained.
This conclusion challenges the basis of certitude from miracles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزعم بعضهم أن نوع ما أتى به النبي عن الدليل مما يمكن تحصيله لمن له في نوعه تكلف واجتهاد وفي بابه تدرب واعتياد وهؤلاء الذين ادعى مدعى الرسالة رسالته فيهم لعلهم لم يكن لهم في ذلك اعتياد، ولم يمتحن مدعي الرسالة قوى جميع البشر، ولعله لو امتحن لوجد من يقدر على مثله ويعارضه في صنعه، ومع تمكن هذا النوع من الإمكان لم يحصل العلم بصدقه ولا المعرفة بصحة رسالته، إذ لا علم مع احتمال البطلان.
And some of them claimed that the kind of evidence that the prophet brought can be acquired by one who has effort and exertion in its kind and training and habituation in its field. And these people among whom the claimant of messengership claimed his messengership perhaps did not have habituation in that, and the claimant of messengership did not test the powers of all humanity, and perhaps if he had tested, he would have found someone who is able to do the like and oppose him in his deed. And with the possibility of this kind, he does not attain certainty about his truthfulness nor knowledge of the correctness of his messengership, since there is no certainty with the possibility of falsehood.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage presents the objection of the third group. They argue that the type of miraculous evidence that a prophet brings can be mastered by anyone who puts in the necessary effort (takalluf), exertion (ijtihād), training (tadarrub), and habituation (i‘tiyād). The prophet's audience may simply be unaccustomed to such feats. The prophet did not test all of humanity; if he had, he might have found someone capable of matching him. Therefore, because there is always the possibility of falsehood (iḥtimāl al-buṭlān), no certain knowledge of his truthfulness can be obtained. This objection attacks the evidential uniqueness of miracles.

Key Terms
تكلف
اجتهاد
تدرب
اعتياد
احتمال البطلان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This argument is a critique of learning or practice in general.
Correction: It is specifically an objection to the exclusive nature of prophetic miracles, not a general condemnation of learning.

Checkpoint
Why does the third group claim that a prophet's miracle does not provide certainty?
A) Because miracles are not real.
B) Because the prophet might have deceived his audience.
C) Because the kind of miracle can be imitated by others with sufficient training, so there is always the possibility of falsehood.
D) Because the prophet did not perform enough miracles.

Key Takeaway
The third group argues that because miracles can be imitated, they do not yield certainty about a prophet's truthfulness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When someone casts doubt on your belief in the Prophet (ﷺ) by claiming that miracles can be learned, does your certainty waver? What evidence do you truly rely on — intellectual proof or the inner conviction that comes from faith? Pause and ask yourself: if you needed to defend the truth of prophethood to a skeptic using only the arguments from this lesson, would you be able to? Commit to studying the proofs of prophethood until your certainty is unshakable.
?
Have you ever dismissed a miracle as simply an extraordinary skill acquired through practice? This lesson forces you to examine the weight you give to possibilities. Are you willing to base your entire faith on a possibility of falsehood? Or will you seek the certainty that comes from real evidence? Today, reflect on one miracle of the Prophet (ﷺ) that you know well and ask: 'Is my belief in this miracle grounded in solid proof, or in hearsay?' Resolve to learn one proof so deeply that no doubt can shake it.
?
The third group's objection rests on the claim that the prophet did not test all of humanity. But you have not tested all possibilities either. Is your skepticism about miracles really intellectual honesty, or a convenient excuse to avoid commitment? This question is uncomfortable: Are you hiding behind hypothetical possibilities to avoid submitting to the truth? Decide right now: will you accept the truth once you see clear evidence, or will you keep moving the goalposts?

The Argument That Prophets' Claims Are Impossible Because Their Commands Are Foolish
The fourth group argues that prophets' claims are impossible because their commands are foolish.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a group of deniers argues that although miracles are possible in principle, the specific teachings of the prophets are themselves irrational, making prophethood impossible.

Core Idea
Deniers admit God can do miracles, but say prophetic commands are absurd, so prophethood is impossible.

This passage presents a unique objection from skeptics who accept divine power but reject prophethood on the grounds that the teachings of the prophets are foolish. They list several Islamic rituals as examples of irrational commands. As you read, notice how they try to turn the argument of miracles on its head.

Guided Path
1
Understand the deniers' concession
Notice that the deniers first concede that miracles are possible and permissible in wisdom. They do not deny God's ability to perform wonders.
This is important because they are not atheists; they affirm the existence of the Maker.
2
Identify their accusation of foolishness
They argue that the specific claims of the prophets are impossible and absurd. They claim that the prophets' commands are outside wisdom and enter into foolishness.
They use the phrase 'خارجة عن الحكمة داخلة في حيز السفه'.
3
See the list of examples
Read the list of Islamic practices they cite as proof of foolishness, such as wudu, Hajj rituals, and touching the Black Stone. Reflect on why a skeptical outsider might find them irrational.
Remember these are the deniers' objections, not the author's views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن المنكرين للرسالة من زعم أن لا خلل في جانب الإمكان بل هي ممكنة جائزة في الحكمة إلا أن جميع ما ادعاها وأتى بالدلالة عليها كان دعواه ممتنعا محالاً، ونقض العادة مما لا يدل على صحة المحال، فكان نقض العادة وقلب الطبيعة جاريًا مجرى الشبه دون الحجج إذ لا حجة تقوم على تصحيح المحال، ولهذا جوزتم ظهور الناقض للمادة على يدي المتأله مع امتناع دعواه وزعمتم أن ذلك من باب الشبه دون الحجج لما أنه لا تصحيح للمحال بالحجة فكذا هذا، قالوا: ودليل كون دعواهم ممتنعا أنهم أتوا بأشياء خارجة عن الحكمة داخلة في حيز السفه من نحو إيجاب غسل الوجه واليدين والرجلين والمسح على الرأس عند خروج الحدث من محل مخصوص، مع الإعفاء عن غسل محل خروج الحجر لا إلى أحد في الحج، والعدو بين الأماكن، وهز الكتفين وتحريك الأعضاء من غير حضور أحد يرآيه الفاعل، واستلام الحجر أصم لا ينفع [؟] النجاسة، ورمى [؟] ولا يضر وغير ذلك من المطاعن لهم ، أعرضنا عن ذكرها لشهرتها. هذا هو بيان لفرق المنكرين للرسالة مع إقرارهم بثبوت الصانع.
And among the deniers of the message are those who claimed that there is no flaw in the aspect of possibility, rather it is possible and permissible in wisdom, except that everything that [the prophets] claimed and brought as evidence for it was an impossible and absurd claim. And the breaking of custom does not indicate the correctness of the absurd. So the breaking of custom and overturning of nature proceed in the manner of ambiguities (shubah) rather than proofs, since no proof can be established for the correction of the absurd. And for this reason you permitted the occurrence of the extraordinary [miracle] upon the hands of the devotee (mutā'allih) while his claim is impossible, and you claimed that is from the category of ambiguities, not proofs, because there is no correction of the absurd by proof. Similarly for this. They said: The proof that their claims are impossible is that they came with things outside of wisdom, entering into foolishness, such as obligating washing of the face, hands, feet, and wiping the head when a specific impurity emanates from a specific place, while exempting from washing the place of exit of the stone [?], throwing [?] to no one in Hajj, running between places, shaking the shoulders, moving limbs without anyone present seeing the doer, touching a deaf stone that neither benefits [?] ritual impurity [?], nor harms, and other objections against them. We refrained from mentioning them due to their notoriety. This is an exposition of the groups of deniers of prophethood while they affirm the existence of the Maker.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage presents the objection of the fourth group of deniers. They accept that God can perform miracles (no flaw in possibility), but they argue that the specific claims of the prophets are themselves impossible (mumtani‘) and absurd (muḥāl). The breaking of custom (naqḍ al-‘ādah) does not prove the absurd. They compare this to the case of a devotee (mutā'allih) who performs marvels but whose claim is rejected as absurd. Then they list several Islamic practices (e.g., wudu, Hajj rituals, prayer movements, kissing the Black Stone) that they consider irrational and foolish, thus proving the impossibility of the prophets' claims. The author notes he refrains from elaborating due to the notoriety of these objections. He concludes by stating that this is an exposition of the various groups of deniers who still affirm the existence of God.

Key Terms
الإمكان
الحكمة
المحال
الشبه
المطاعن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The list of Islamic practices is presented as the author's criticism of Islam.
Correction: The list is given as the deniers' objection; the author is reporting their view, not endorsing it.

Checkpoint
What do the fourth group of deniers cite as evidence that the prophets' claims are impossible?
A) The prophets performed no miracles.
B) The prophets' teachings include commands that appear foolish or irrational.
C) The prophets contradicted each other.
D) The prophets were not wise.

Key Takeaway
The fourth group of deniers accepts divine power but rejects prophethood by claiming that the teachings of prophets are absurd, using specific Islamic rituals as examples.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform acts like wudu, prayer, or Hajj, do you ever feel they are meaningless routines? How does knowing that the deniers used these very acts to reject prophethood affect your view of them? Will you now approach them as signs of divine wisdom or let the deniers' doubt creep in?
?
The deniers accepted God's existence and power but rejected His messenger because they found the commands unreasonable. Is there any prophetic command that you struggle to see the wisdom in? How does this lesson challenge you to submit even when you don't understand?
?
If someone today claimed that Islamic rituals are foolish and therefore the Prophet (peace be upon him) cannot be true, how would you respond not just with intellect but with spiritual conviction? What in your own heart needs to be strengthened so that you are not shaken by such objections?

The First Objection: Miracles Are Not Inimitable
Nasafi presents the first objection: miracles are reproducible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first argument used by those who deny prophethood while affirming God: that miracles could potentially be reproduced by others, thus undermining certainty in the prophet's truthfulness.

Core Idea
Miracles lose their proof value if they can be imitated by any trained human.

Imam Nasafi begins by presenting the first of two objections from people who accept a Creator but reject prophethood. They argue that the miracles prophets bring are not unique; with enough effort and training, anyone could produce similar feats. This objection challenges the very basis of using miracles as proofs of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the objection's flow.
Focus on the key claim: the miracle type is acquirable.
2
Identify the core claim
The objectors claim that the miracle brought by the prophet is something that can be acquired by anyone with effort and training.
3
Reflect on why this undermines certainty
The objectors argue that since the prophet did not test all mankind, someone might be able to replicate the miracle, so we cannot be certain of his truthfulness.
This leads to the conclusion that miracles do not provide certain knowledge of prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزعم بعضهم أن نوع ما أتى به النبي عن الدليل مما يمكن تحصيله لمن له في نوعه تكلف واجتهاد وفي بابه تدرب واعتياد وهؤلاء الذين ادعى مدعى الرسالة رسالته فيهم لعلهم لم يكن لهم في ذلك اعتياد ولم يمتحن مدعي الرسالة قوى جميع البشر، ولعله لو امتحن لوجد من يقدر على مثله ويعارضه في صنعه، ومع تمكن هذا النوع من الإمكان لم يحصل العلم بصدقه ولا المعرفة بصحة رسالته، إذ لا علم مع احتمال البطلان. ومن المنكرين للرسالة من زعم أن لا خلل في جانب الإمكان بل هي ممكنة جائزة في الحكمة إلا أن جميع ما ادعاها وأتى بالدلالة عليها كان دعواه ممتنعا محالاً، ونقض العادة مما لا يدل على صحة المحال، فكان نقض العادة وقلب الطبيعة جاريًا مجرى الشبه دون الحجج إذ لا حجة تقوم على تصحيح المحال، ولهذا جوزتم ظهور الناقض للمادة على يدي المتأله مع امتناع دعواه وزعمتم أن ذلك من باب الشبه دون الحجج لما أنه لا تصحيح للمحال بالحجة فكذا هذا، قالوا: ودليل كون دعواهم ممتنعا أنهم أتوا بأشياء خارجة عن الحكمة داخلة في حيز السفه من نحو إيجاب غسل الوجه واليدين والرجلين والمسح على الرأس عند خروج الحدث من محل مخصوص، مع الإعفاء عن غسل محل خروج الحجر لا إلى أحد في الحج، والعدو بين الأماكن، وهز الكتفين وتحريك الأعضاء من غير حضور أحد يرآيه الفاعل، واستلام الحجر أصم لا ينفع النجاسة، ورمى لا يضر وغير ذلك من المطاعن لهم، أعرضنا عن ذكرها لشهرتها. هذا هو بيان لفرق المنكرين للرسالة مع إقرارهم بثبوت الصانع.
And some have claimed that the type (of miracle) that the prophet brought as proof is something that can be acquired by anyone who undertakes effort and exertion in its kind and is trained and accustomed in its field. And these people to whom the claimant of prophethood claimed his prophethood, perhaps they had no familiarity in that, and the claimant of prophethood did not test the powers of all mankind. Perhaps if he had tested, he would have found someone capable of producing its like and opposing him in his act. And with the possibility of this kind being possible, certainty of his truthfulness is not attained nor knowledge of the validity of his prophethood, for there is no knowledge with the possibility of falsehood. And among the deniers of prophethood is one who claimed that there is no defect in the aspect of possibility; rather it is possible and permissible in wisdom, but all that he claimed and brought as evidence for it, his claim is impossible and absurd. And the breaking of custom does not indicate the validity of the impossible. So the breaking of custom and the overturning of nature are in the category of dubious arguments (shubah) rather than proofs, since no proof stands for validating the impossible. And for this reason you (theologians) permit the occurrence of a custom-breaker at the hands of an ascetic (mutā'allih) despite the impossibility of his claim, and you claim that this is from the category of shubah not proofs, because there is no validation of the impossible by proof. So likewise this. They said: The proof that their claim is impossible is that they brought things outside wisdom, within the realm of folly, such as obligating washing the face, hands, feet, and wiping the head upon exiting a hadath from a specific place, while exempting washing the place of exit of the stone for nothing in Hajj, and running between places, and shaking the shoulders and moving limbs without the presence of anyone seeing the doer, and kissing the black stone which is deaf and does not benefit against impurity, and throwing (stones) which neither harms nor benefits, and other objections against them. We have refrained from mentioning them due to their notoriety. This is the statement of the groups of deniers of prophethood while they affirm the existence of the Creator.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage presents two distinct objections raised by those who deny prophethood while still affirming the existence of God. The first objection argues that the miracles brought by prophets are not inherently inimitable; with sufficient training and effort, others could potentially produce similar feats. Since the prophet did not test all of humanity, the possibility remains that someone could match his miracle, thus undermining certainty in his truthfulness. The second objection concedes that miracles are possible in themselves but insists that the prophetic claim itself is impossible because it involves irrational legislation—such as detailed purification rituals, Hajj rites like running and throwing stones, and kissing a lifeless stone—which contradict wisdom and are deemed foolish. The objectors argue that breaking natural custom (naqd al-ʿāda) does not validate an impossible claim; rather, such miracles are mere dubious arguments (shubah), not proofs. They compare this to the theologians' own view that miracles at the hands of ascetics are shubah, not proofs. The passage concludes that these are the arguments of those who reject prophets but accept God.

Key Terms
إمكان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These objectors are atheists who deny God.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that they affirm the existence of the Creator.

Checkpoint
According to the first objection, why do miracles not prove prophethood?
A) Miracles break natural laws.
B) Miracles could be reproduced by others.
C) Miracles are only illusions.
D) Prophets themselves are not sure.

Key Takeaway
The first objection claims that miracles are not unique proofs because they could be performed by anyone with sufficient training, so they do not yield certainty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself doubting a clear sign from Allah because you thought it could be explained by human effort or coincidence? What does that say about your heart's reliance on certainty?
?
The objection claims that since the prophet did not test all of humanity, there might be an imitator. In your life, do you wait for absolute proof before committing to faith, or do you act on the overwhelming signs already given?
?
If someone today raised this same objection to you, would you be able to refute it from the Qur'an and Sunnah? What is your responsibility to equip yourself with knowledge against such doubts?

The Second Objection: Prophetic Laws Are Irrational and Impossible
Nasafi presents the second objection: prophetic laws are irrational so the claim is impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second objection: that even if miracles are possible, the specific claims and laws of prophets are absurd and contradict wisdom, so the prophetic claim is impossible.

Core Idea
Prophetic laws that seem foolish render the whole claim impossible, no matter the miracle.

The second objection goes further: even if we accept that miracles are possible, the actual content of the prophet's message—the detailed rituals and practices—appears irrational and outside wisdom. This, the objectors argue, proves that the prophetic claim itself is impossible, and miracles cannot validate an impossible claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage for the second objection
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the concessive start: 'no defect in possibility'.
The objection concedes miracles are possible but attacks the content of the message.
2
Understand the claim: the laws are foolish
The objectors list specific Islamic practices they consider irrational, calling them 'outside wisdom' and 'folly'.
Examples include wudu, Hajj rituals like running and throwing stones, etc.
3
See the comparison with ascetics' miracles
The objectors analogize: just as theologians dismiss miracles at the hands of ascetics as shubah (not proofs), so should the prophets' miracles be dismissed because the claim is impossible.
This shows internal contradiction in the theologians' position.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever looked at a command of Allah or His Prophet and thought in your heart, 'This doesn't make sense' or 'This is foolish'? What does this lesson reveal about the danger of judging divine legislation by your own limited wisdom? Will you submit to every command from now on, even the ones you don't understand?
?
The objectors conceded miracles are possible but still rejected prophethood because they found the laws irrational. If you have ever doubted the wisdom of a particular Islamic practice (e.g., wudu, Hajj rituals), how does this lesson challenge that doubt? Are you willing to trust Allah's wisdom over your own?
?
The objectors used the principle that miracles cannot prove an impossible claim. You likely accept that principle for false prophets. Does your belief in the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) rest on miracles alone, or is it also grounded in the content of his message being from God? If someone questioned a specific law, how would your faith hold up?

Prophethood
beginner
5 min
Method of Argument with Different Deniers of Prophethood
Imam Nasafi outlines the proper method of argument with different types of prophethood deniers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi tailors the argument for prophethood based on the opponent's prior denial of the Creator or of khabar (news) as a source of knowledge.

Core Idea
Different deniers require different starting points: prove the Creator first, or prove khabar as knowledge.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi distinguishes between two types of deniers of prophethood. With those who deny the Creator entirely, the discussion must first establish God's existence. With groups like the Sumaniyya and Barahima who deny prophethood because they reject the epistemic value of transmitted news (khabar), the initial argument must focus on proving that khabar is indeed a valid source of knowledge. This shows a methodical approach: address the foundational issue before the specific proof of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the contrast Imam Nasafi makes between two groups.
2
Identify the two types of deniers
The passage names two categories: those who deny the Creator, and those who deny prophethood from among the Sumaniyya and Barahima. Note how each is handled.
The second group denies prophethood because they reject khabar as a source of knowledge.
3
Understand the method for each
For the first group, the discussion must start with proving the Creator. For the second, the initial discussion is about establishing khabar as a means of knowledge, not about prophethood directly.
Imam Nasafi references earlier material that already suffices for proving khabar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من أنكر الصانع فهو منكر للرسالة إذ القول بالرسول ولا مرسل محالاً. إلا أن الكلام معهم يقع في إثبات الصانع. وكذا من أنكر الرسالة من السمنية والبراهمة لما أن الخبر ليس من أسباب المصارف فلا يفيد خبر الرسول معنى فلا فائدة في إرساله. لا نتكلم معه في هذه المسألة ابتداء بل نتكلم فى إثبات كون الخبر سببًا من أسباب المعارف، وقد مر في أول الكتاب ما يقع الفنية به بحمد الله تعالى.
As for whoever denies the Creator, there is no doubt that he denies prophethood, because the statement 'a messenger with no sender' is impossible. However, the discussion with them occurs in proving the Creator. Likewise, whoever denies prophethood from among the Sumaniyya and the Barahima, because news (khabar) is not among the means of knowledge, so the news of a messenger yields no meaning, so there is no benefit in sending him. We do not speak with him in this issue initially; rather we speak in proving that news (khabar) is a cause among the causes of knowledge, and it has already passed at the beginning of the book what suffices, by the praise of God.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
In this passage, Imam Nasafi distinguishes between two types of deniers of prophethood. First, those who deny the Creator altogether: with them, one must first prove God's existence, because a messenger without a sender is absurd. Second, groups like the Sumaniyya and Barahima who deny prophethood because they reject that news (khabar) can be a source of knowledge. With them, the initial discussion is not about prophethood but about establishing that khabar is indeed a means of knowledge—a topic already covered earlier in the book. This shows the author's methodical approach: address the foundational epistemological issue before engaging in the specific proof of prophethood.

Key Terms
الصانع
السمنية
البراهمة
الخبر
أسباب المعارف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that deniers of the Creator can be argued with about prophethood directly, without first proving God's existence.
Correction: Imam Nasafi clarifies that arguing about a messenger without establishing a sender is impossible; one must first prove the Creator.

Checkpoint
How does Imam Nasafi respond to those who deny prophethood because they reject khabar as a source of knowledge?
A) He proves prophethood directly using miracles.
B) He first proves that khabar is a source of knowledge.
C) He dismisses their argument as irrelevant.
D) He argues that even without khabar, reason suffices.

Key Takeaway
The method of arguing for prophethood depends on the opponent's prior denial—prove the Creator for atheists, prove khabar as knowledge for epistemologically skeptical groups.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter someone who rejects a truth because they reject the method of transmission (like the Sumaniyya reject khabar), do you get frustrated or do you first address their epistemology? How can you train yourself to pause and identify the real root of their denial before arguing? Commit to doing this in your next conversation about faith.
?
Have you ever found yourself arguing about a higher-level issue (like prophethood) when the person you're speaking with hasn't accepted the foundational truths (like God's existence) that make that issue meaningful? How might you adjust your approach to be more effective? Write down one specific change you will make.
?
This passage teaches that different deniers require different starting points. Are there areas in your own life where you have been treating everyone the same way, instead of tailoring your approach? How can you begin to assess each person's unique obstacles to belief and meet them where they are, as a form of sincere concern for their guidance?

Prophethood

The Possibility of Prophethood: God's Absolute Ownership
Al-Nasafi proves the rational possibility of prophethood by appealing to God's absolute ownership.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Nasafi's argument for the rational possibility of prophethood based on God's absolute ownership and authority.

Core Idea
Prophethood is possible because the absolute Owner has full authority over His property.

Before discussing whether prophethood actually occurred, al-Nasafi first establishes that it is rationally possible. In this passage, he argues that since God is the absolute Owner and Creator of everything, He has the right to impose obligations and send messengers. This argument clears the ground for later proofs of the necessity and actuality of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prerequisite
The passage first specifies that opponents must already affirm God's existence and attributes; otherwise, the discussion about prophethood cannot proceed.
Al-Nasafi insists on prior agreement on God's oneness and ownership.
2
Understand the key analogy
Recognize that the argument uses the analogy of an owner's right to dispose of property to show that God's authority includes sending messengers.
Every owner has authority over his property; God's ownership is absolute.
3
Note the exclusive divine ownership
Observe that al-Nasafi emphasizes milk al-takhliq — God's ownership of creation from nothing — which grounds His absolute authority.
This is a unique type of ownership not shared by any creature.
4
Consider the modes of communication
The passage explains that God can inform His servants of obligations either by direct creation of knowledge or by sending a messenger, and both are equally possible.
The mode does not affect the possibility of prophethood itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرسالة ممكنة]: أما الكلام في الإمكان فنقول: إن خصماءنا في باب الرسالة هم المقرون بالصانع الحكيم الواحد الفرد الذي لا يشركه أحد في ألوهيته، ولا يخرج شيء من المحدثات عن ملكه وقهره، وأنه هو المالك وما سواه مملوك، وهو الرب وما عداه فأما مربوب. من خالفنا في شيء من هذه الفصول فأنكر حدوث العالم أو ثبوت الصانع أو وحدانيته فلا كلام معه في فصل الرسالة، بل الواجب إثبات ذلك عليه بالدلائل على ما بينا. وإذا كان الأمر كذلك وكان الاعتراف من خصمائنا بذلك كله سابقا نقول: إن ورود التكليف بالإيجاب والحظر والإطلاق والمنع ممن له الملك في مماليكه ليس مما تأباه العقول ولا مما تدفعه الدلائل، إذ لكل مالك ولاية التصرف في مملوكه بقدر ما له من الملك فيه، والله تعالى في كل جزء من أجزاء العالم وشخص من أشخاص بني آدم ملك التخليق، إذ هو الموجد له عن العدم المخترع له لا عن أصل، فكان له أن يتصرف في كل من ذلك بأي وجه شاء من وجوه التصرف منعًا كان أو إطلاقا، حظرًا كان أو إيجابًا، ثم يعلمهم ذلك بأي طريق شاء، إن شاء بتخليقه العلم بذلك التكليف، وإن شاء بإرسال رسول يوحى إليه ذلك، ويأمره بالتبليغ إلى العقلاء المميزين من عباده، كان ذلك الرسول من جنس المرسل إليهم أو من خلاف جنسهم، ولا يستحيل ذلك منه إذ هو المتصرف في مُلْكه وملكه، وما هذا سبيله فلا استحالة في نفسه، فلو استحال لاستحال لمعنى يقترن به.
[Prophethood is possible]: As for the discussion of possibility, we say: Our opponents in the matter of prophethood are those who affirm the Wise Creator, the One, the Unique, whom none shares in His divinity, nothing phenomenal escapes His dominion and power, and that He is the Owner (al-Malik) and whatever besides Him is owned, and He is the Lord (al-Rabb) and whatever besides Him is subjugated. Whoever opposes us in any of these points, denying the temporal origination of the world, or the existence of the Creator, or His Oneness, then there is no discussion with him on the matter of prophethood; rather, it is obligatory to prove those things to him by proofs, as we have explained. When the matter is so and our opponents have already admitted all this, we say: The imposition of obligation (taklif) by command and prohibition, permission and restriction, from one who has ownership over his servants, is not something that intellects reject nor do proofs refute. For every owner has authority to dispose of his property according to the extent of his ownership in it. And God Almighty, in every part of the world and every individual human being, has the ownership of creation (milk al-takhliq), for He is the one who brings it into existence from non-existence, inventing it not from an origin. So He has the right to dispose of each of these in any way He wills of modes of disposition, whether prohibition or permission, restriction or obligation. Then He informs them of that by any means He wills: if He wills, by creating in them knowledge of that obligation; and if He wills, by sending a messenger who is inspired with that and commanded to convey it to the intelligent, discerning servants. That messenger could be of the same kind as those sent to or of a different kind. And that is not impossible from Him, for He is the disposer in His dominion and property. Whatever is like this, there is no impossibility in itself. If it were impossible, it would be impossible due to some concomitant meaning.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage is a proof of the possibility (imkān) of prophethood. Al-Nasafi begins by specifying the opponents: they must already affirm the existence and attributes of God (Creator, One, Owner, Lord). If they deny these, the discussion must first establish these foundational beliefs. Assuming they do affirm them, he argues that God, as the absolute owner (al-Mālik) and creator of everything, has the right to impose obligations (taklīf) on His servants and to communicate those obligations by any means He chooses, whether by direct creation of knowledge or by sending a messenger. There is no intellectual objection to this, as it is analogous to any owner's right to dispose of his property. God's ownership is perfect (milk al-takhliq), as He creates from nothing. Therefore, sending a messenger is not intrinsically impossible; if it were, the impossibility would have to arise from some external factor, which is not the case. This argument establishes the rational possibility of prophethood before discussing its necessity or actual occurrence.

Key Terms
الإمكان
التكليف
الملك
ملك التخليق
التصرف
الوجوب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophethood's possibility is proven only after it has occurred.
Correction: Al-Nasafi argues that prophethood is rationally possible prior to and independent of its actual occurrence, based on God's absolute ownership.

Checkpoint
What is the key reason al-Nasafi gives for the possibility of God sending a messenger?
A) Because messengers are always of the same kind as people.
B) Because God is the absolute owner and creator, so He has the right to impose obligations and communicate them.
C) Because all intellects demand it.
D) Because it is a well-known historical fact.

Key Takeaway
Prophethood is rationally possible because God, as the absolute Owner and Creator, has full authority to impose obligations and send messengers to His creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself questioning the fairness of God's commandments, do you remember that He is the absolute Owner of your existence? How does the truth that you are His property change your attitude towards His commands? Write one command you have been resisting and commit to obeying it as a matter of ownership, not preference.
?
This lesson argues that God can choose any means to communicate with us, including sending a messenger. Do you treat the Prophet Muhammad (s) as the authoritative messenger from your Owner, or do you pick and choose what you accept from him? What would change if you genuinely believed that his message is your Owner's direct instruction to you?
?
If God, as Owner, has the right to impose any obligation, why do you feel burdened by the duties of Islam? Could it be that you have forgotten that you are owned? Reflect on your daily life: are there any moments when you act as if you are self-owned rather than owned by God? How can you remind yourself of this reality tomorrow?

Prophethood

Establishing the Possibility of Prophethood
Al-Nasafi argues for the possibility of prophethood based on divine ownership and wisdom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational basis for the possibility of prophethood, grounded in divine ownership and wisdom.

Core Idea
Prophethood is possible because God owns all things and is wise.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi's Tabsirat al-Adilla lays the foundation for the discussion of prophethood. Before proving its actual occurrence, we must first establish that prophethood is rationally possible. Al-Nasafi argues that if God exists as the sole Creator and Owner of all, then He has the authority to impose obligations and send messengers. This lesson unpacks that argument and its supporting premises.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Begin by reading the full Arabic passage and its literal translation. Pay attention to the flow of the argument and the key terms.
The passage is dense, so read it twice: once for overall meaning, once for details.
2
Identify the opponents in the discussion
Al-Nasafi specifies that his opponents are those who already affirm a wise Creator and His absolute ownership. Note that those who deny these fundamentals are not addressed here.
This sets the stage for a focused argument with shared premises.
3
Trace the ownership argument
The core argument: God owns everything, so He has the right to impose obligations (taklif) and send messengers. Follow the logical steps from ownership to possibility.
Key concept: ownership implies authority to dispose; this is not intellectually impossible.
4
Understand the supporting arguments
Al-Nasafi reinforces the main argument by noting that human nature is receptive to guidance and that God's wisdom and mercy make sending messengers appropriate.
This shows that not only is prophethood possible, but it is also expected from a wise and merciful God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فنتكلم في إثبات إمكانها أولاً ثم نتكلم في الاختلاف في وجوبها بين المتكلمين. ثم نتكلم في إقامة الدلالة على ثبوتها، ونأتي في كل فصل بما يوجب صحته من الدلائل - إن شاء الله تعالى. أما الكلام في الإمكان فنقول: إن خصماءنا في باب الرسالة هم المقرون بالصانع الحكيم الواحد الفرد الذي لا يشركه أحد في ألوهيته، ولا يخرج شيء من المحدثات عن ملكه وقهره، وأنه هو المالك وما سواه مملوك، وهو الرب وما عداه فأما مربوب. من خالفنا في شيء من هذه الفصول فأنكر حدوث العالم أو ثبوت الصانع أو وحدانيته فلا كلام معه في فصل الرسالة، بل الواجب إثبات ذلك عليه بالدلائل على ما بينا. وإذا كان الأمر كذلك وكان الاعتراف من خصمائنا بذلك كله سابقا نقول : إن ورود التكليف بالإيجاب والحظر والإطلاق والمنع ممن له الملك في مماليكه ليس مما تأباه العقول ولا مما تدفعه الدلائل، إذ لكل مالك ولاية التصرف في مملوكه بقدر ما له من الملك فيه، والله تعالى في كل جزء من أجزاء العالم وشخص من أشخاص بني آدم ملك التخليق، إذ هو الموجد له عن العدم المخترع له لا عن أصل، فكان له أن يتصرف في كل من ذلك بأي وجه شاء من وجوه التصرف منعاً كان أو إطلاقا، حظراً كان أو إيجاباً، ثم يعلمهم ذلك بأي طريق شاء، إن شاء بتخليقه العلم بذلك التكليف، وإن شاء بإرسال رسول يوحى إليه ذلك، ويأمره بالتبليغ إلى العقلاء المميزين من عباده، كان ذلك الرسول من جنس المرسل إليهم أو من خلاف جنسهم، ولا يستحيل ذلك منه إذ هو المتصرف في مُلْكه وملكه، وما هذا سبيله فلا استحالة في نفسه، فلو استحال لاستحال لمعنى يقترن به لا لنفسه، وهذا مما لا شك فيه لمن عقل وأنصف من نفسه. والذي يؤيد هذا أن الجبلة البشرية مهيأة لقبول الحكم والعلوم معدة للزيادة وبلوغ درجة الكمال فيها عند إفادة الحكيم المرشد إياها، إذ هي ليست ممن لا يجوز عليه الجهل بالأشياء، ولا مما يمتنع عليه قبول العلوم والحكم مع تفنن أقسامها وتكثر أعدادها. ثم لا شك أن صانع العالم حكيم لا يسفه عليم لا يجهل، ومن هذا وصفه، فليس بممتنع منه إمداد المجبول على النقيصة بما يوجب زوالها عنه ويورث له الكمال وبلوغ الدرجة العالية في العلم والحكمة، بل هو من الممكن الذي جرت به العادة من الموسومين بالحكمة المشهورين بالتحلي بالعلوم إذ لم يخل عصر من الأعصار ممن يقوم من العلماء لإفادة ما سعد به من العلم المحتاجين إليه العارين عنه ليبلغوا ببركته الكمال وتندفع عنهم نقيصة الجهل بذلك. فالله تعالى مع كمال حكمته ورحمته على عبادة أولى أن لا يمتنع منه ذلك.
We will speak first about establishing its possibility, then we will speak about the disagreement regarding its obligatoriness among the theologians. Then we will speak about establishing the proof of its existence, and we will bring in each chapter what necessitates its correctness from proofs — if God wills. As for the discourse on possibility, we say: Our opponents in the matter of prophethood are those who affirm the wise, one, solitary Maker, whom no one shares in His divinity, and no originated thing escapes His dominion and subjugation, and that He is the Owner and what is other than Him is owned, and He is the Lord and whatever is other than Him is a thing that is lorded over. Whoever opposes us in any of these matters by denying the originatedness of the world, or the existence of the Maker, or His oneness, then there is no discourse with him concerning the matter of prophethood; rather, it is obligatory to establish that against him by proofs, as we have explained. And since the matter is so, and the acknowledgment from our opponents of all that is prior, we say: The occurrence of obligation by command, prohibition, permission, and restriction from one who has ownership over his owned things is not something that intellects reject nor that proofs repel, for every owner has authority to dispose of his owned property to the extent of his ownership in it, and God Almighty has, in every part of the world and every individual human being, ownership of creation, for He is the one who brings it into existence from non-existence, inventing it without any pre-existing substance. So He may dispose of each of that in any manner He wills of the modes of disposal, whether prohibition or permission, restriction or command, then inform them of that by any means He wills, whether by creating in them knowledge of that obligation, or by sending a messenger who is inspired with that and commanded to convey it to the rational, discerning among His servants, whether that messenger be of the same species as those to whom he is sent or of a different species. And that is not impossible from Him, for He is the disposer in His kingdom and property, and what is of this way has no impossibility in itself; if it were impossible, it would be impossible due to something incidental to it, not due to itself. And this is something about which there is no doubt for one who reasons and is fair to himself. And what supports this is that human nature is prepared to accept wisdom and sciences, disposed for increase and reaching the degree of perfection in them upon the instruction of the wise guide, for it is not among those for whom ignorance of things is impossible, nor among those for whom acceptance of sciences and wisdom is impossible despite the diversity of their kinds and the multiplicity of their numbers. Then there is no doubt that the Maker of the world is wise, not foolish, knowing, not ignorant. And He whose attribute is such, it is not impossible for Him to supply what is created upon deficiency with what necessitates its removal from him and gives him perfection and attainment of the high degree in knowledge and wisdom. Rather, it is among the possible things that is customary among those characterized by wisdom and famous for adorning themselves with sciences, for no age has been devoid of those among the scholars who stand to impart the knowledge they have been blessed with to those in need of it and devoid of it, so that through his blessing they may attain perfection and the deficiency of ignorance be repelled from them. So God Almighty, with the perfection of His wisdom and mercy towards His servants, is more worthy that it should not be impossible from Him.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the possibility (imkan) of prophethood (risala). Al-Nasafi begins by outlining the structure of the discussion: first establishing possibility, then the disagreement about obligatoriness (wujub), then the proof of actual occurrence. He then directly addresses the possibility. He states that his opponents in this matter are theists who already affirm a single, wise Creator who owns all things. If someone denies these fundamentals (origination of the world, existence of God, His oneness), then there is no point debating prophethood with them until those are proven. Given that the opponent agrees on divine ownership and lordship, the argument proceeds: the owner has full authority to dispose of his property. God's ownership includes every part of the universe and every human being, as He is the sole creator. Therefore, He may impose obligations (taklif) such as commands, prohibitions, permissions, and restrictions on His servants in any manner He chooses. He may also inform them of these obligations by any means—either by creating direct knowledge in them or by sending a messenger. The messenger could be of the same species or a different one; none of this is impossible for God because He is the absolute disposer of His kingdom. If it were impossible, it would be due to some external factor, not because of an inherent absurdity. Al-Nasafi then reinforces this by appealing to human nature: humans are naturally receptive to learning and wisdom, and they can increase in knowledge through the instruction of a wise guide. Since God is wise and not foolish, it is not impossible for Him to supply deficient humans with what perfects them. In fact, it is analogous to the customary practice of wise scholars teaching others. Thus, given God's perfect wisdom and mercy, it is even more fitting that He would not refrain from sending messengers.

Key Terms
الإمكان (imkan)
التكليف (taklif)
الرسالة (risala)
المالك (al-malik)
المملوك (al-mamluk)
الحكيم (al-hakim)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think prophethood is impossible because it imposes obligations without benefit to God, or because it is beneath His majesty.
Correction: Al-Nasafi clarifies that possibility is based on divine ownership and wisdom, not on benefit to God. God owns all, so He may dispose as He wills, and His wisdom necessitates guidance for His servants.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Nasafi, who are the opponents in the discussion of prophethood?
A) Atheists who deny God altogether
B) Those who affirm a wise Creator who owns all things
C) Only Muslims
D) Those who deny the possibility of miracles

Key Takeaway
The possibility of prophethood is rationally established because God, as the absolute Owner and Wise Creator, has the authority to communicate obligations to His servants through messengers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live as if God, your absolute Owner, has the right to command and prohibit you through His messengers? If you accept His ownership, why do you still hesitate to obey His commands, and what will you change today to align your life with that conviction?
?
Al-Nasafi argues that human nature is prepared for perfection through instruction. Where in your life are you actively seeking that instruction from the Prophet (peace be upon him)? What specific step will you take this week to increase your knowledge of his teachings?
?
If God is wise and merciful, and He perfects His creation by sending messengers, then what excuse do you have for neglecting the final message He sent? How does your daily routine reflect—or fail to reflect—your belief that the Prophet (peace be upon him) is the ultimate guide?

Prophethood
intermediate
6 min
The Rational Basis for Prophethood
Al-Nasafi argues that human nature is prepared for knowledge and that God's wisdom necessitates sending messengers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument for why God, in His wisdom and mercy, sends messengers to guide humanity.

Core Idea
Human nature is made for knowledge; God's wisdom sends guides to perfect it.

Imam al-Nasafi here builds a rational case for prophethood. He argues that human nature is inherently disposed to learn and grow, and that a wise and merciful Creator would not leave this nature without guidance. This lesson walks through his argument from human nature to divine attributes to the necessity of sending messengers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Let the author's argument unfold naturally.
Notice the author's use of logical reasoning and appeal to consensus.
2
Identify the core argument
Al-Nasafi first establishes that human nature is ready for knowledge, then argues that God's wisdom requires providing guidance to remove deficiency.
This is a key theological move from human potential to divine obligation.
3
Analyze the conditions for sending messengers
The author lists several conditions that show sending messengers does not conflict with God's attributes or justice. Identify each condition and its significance.
These conditions defend against possible objections.
4
Reflect on the consensus of previous religions
Al-Nasafi uses the agreement of Jews, Christians, and Muslims on the integrity of their prophets as additional proof. Consider why this strengthens his argument.
This consensus is a historical argument for reliability.
