وجه الحاجة إلى بيان الواجب والممتنع] على أن الحاجة ماسة في قسمي الواجب والممتنع اللذين في العقول إمكان الوقوف عليهما في الجملة، إلى البيان الوارد عن الله تعالى لمعنيين: أحدهما يختص ببعض العقلاء. والآخر يشمل الجميع. فأما المعنى الخاص فهو ما مر في أول الكتاب في مسألة إيمان المقلد من انقسام الناس إلى أقسام ثلاثة. أحدهما الموصوفون بحدة الخواطر والأذهان ووفور العقل والألباب، المتفرغون للتأمل والتفكر في المباحث النظرية والمعالم الإلهية، المعرضون عن الذات البهيمية والمطالب الجسمانية. والثاني: الموسومون برجاحة العقول وقوة الخواطر المشتغلون بالمصالح
The aspect of the need for explaining the obligatory and the impossible: Even though in the two categories of the obligatory and the impossible there is possibility of knowing them in general by the intellect, there is still an intense need for the explanation that comes from God Almighty for two reasons: one is specific to some rational people, and the other encompasses all. As for the specific meaning, it is what has passed in the beginning of the book in the issue of the faith of the imitator regarding the division of people into three categories: first, those described as sharpness of thoughts and minds, abundance of intellect and understanding, devoted to contemplation and reflection on theoretical investigations and divine matters, turning away from bestial desires and physical demands. And second, those described as soundness of intellects and strength of thoughts, who are occupied with interests...
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage, though incomplete, explains why revelation is needed even for the categories of wajib (obligatory) and mumtani' (impossible), which reason can know in principle. Nasafi says the need for divine explanation is intense for two reasons: one specific to some rational people, and one general to all. The specific reason refers to a previous discussion in the book about the faith of the imitator, where people are divided into three types. He begins describing the first type: those with sharp intellects and minds, devoted to theoretical and divine matters, detached from base desires and physical concerns. The second type is introduced but cut off: those with sound intellects and strong thoughts, occupied with worldly interests. The passage implies that even those capable of rational knowledge need revelation for confirmation or due to their varying degrees of understanding. The general reason (which is not completed here) presumably applies to everyone.

Misconception: Some think revelation is only needed for possible actions, not for obligatory and impossible acts which reason can know.
Correction: Nasafi shows that even for the obligatory and impossible categories, revelation is needed due to differences in human capacity and engagement.

A) One reason that applies only to the unintelligent.
B) Two reasons: one specific to some rational people, and one general.
C) The impossibility of knowing these categories by reason.

Revelation is needed even for rationally knowable categories because of differences in human intellect and engagement.

Prophethood

Necessity of Messengers to Explain Duties
Author presents a proof for the necessity of prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof for the necessity of prophets based on the need to explain the intermediary category of actions.

Core Idea
Without prophets, we would be permitted to abandon duties and commit sins—contrary to divine wisdom.

This passage presents a concise yet powerful kalam argument for the necessity of prophethood. The author begins with a self-evident premise about human need for guidance on consequences, then shows that denying prophethood leads to a contradiction with divine wisdom. It is a classic example of Maturidi rational theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Let the author's own words sink in before analyzing.
2
Identify the key premise
Find where the author introduces the 'intermediary category' (al-qism al-wāsiṭah) and understand why it requires prophetic explanation.
3
Follow the logical proof
Trace the argument: if no messenger explains this category, then abandoning obligations and committing sins would be permitted, which contradicts divine wisdom. Hence, a messenger is necessary.
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Note that the author concludes that Allah never leaves humanity without a sensory proof (al-ḥujjah al-samʿiyyah) through prophets or their successors.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحاجة إلى بيان من له الاطلاع على عواقب الأمور على لسان من ارتضاه من الرسل ليتمكن من أداء ما وجب منها والامتناع عما حرم، وهذه مقدمة لا خفاء بها على من له أدنى لبس. وقد يمكن أن يجمل عين هذا الكلام دليلاً للقول بوجوب الرسالة، إذ الأمر لما كان على ما بينا فلو لم يرد الوصول ببيان القسم الواسطة وقد يجب منه البعض لتعلق الحميد من العواقب به، ويحرم البعض التعلق الذميم من العواقب به لكان فيه إباحة ترك الواجب وإباحة مباشرة المحظور، وهو خارج عن الحكمة، فلابد من بيان ذلك ممن له العلم بذلك على لسان الرسول ولهذا ما أخلى الله تعالى العالم منذ خلق الممتحنين عن الحجة السمعية. إما على ألسنة الرسل وإما على ألسنة خلفائهم، والله الموفق.
The need is for a statement from one who has knowledge of the consequences of affairs on the tongue of one whom He has chosen from the messengers, so that one may be able to perform what is obligatory from them and refrain from what is forbidden. This is a premise not hidden from anyone who has the least discernment. It is possible that this very statement can be summarized as a proof for the necessity of prophethood. For since the matter is as we have explained, if there were no arrival of a statement concerning the intermediary category—some of which may be obligatory due to the attachment of praiseworthy consequences, and some of which may be prohibited due to the attachment of blameworthy consequences—then it would entail permission to abandon the obligatory and permission to commit the prohibited, which is outside of wisdom. Therefore, a statement of that must come from one who has knowledge of it on the tongue of a messenger. For this reason, Allah the Exalted has not emptied the world, since He created those who are tested, from the sensory proof (al-ḥujjah al-samʿiyyah), either on the tongues of the messengers or on the tongues of their successors. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a concise proof for the necessity of prophethood (wujūb al-risālah). The author begins by stating a clear premise: people need a statement from someone who knows the outcomes of actions, delivered through chosen messengers, to know what to do and what to avoid. This premise is self-evident. He then shows that this same premise can be used as a direct proof: if there were no messenger to explain the 'intermediary category' (al-qism al-wāsiṭah)—actions that can be obligatory or prohibited depending on consequences—then people would be permitted to abandon duties and commit sins, which contradicts divine wisdom. Therefore, a messenger is necessary. The author concludes by noting that Allah has never left the world without a 'sensory proof' (al-ḥujjah al-samʿiyyah), either through prophets or their successors, from the beginning of creation.

Key Terms
وجوب الرسالة
الحجة السمعية
الحكمة
القسم الواسطة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument is circular because it assumes the need for a messenger from the start.
Correction: The argument begins with a universally accepted premise about divine wisdom, not the existence of messengers. It then shows that denying messengers would contradict that premise, thus proving their necessity.

Checkpoint
What would be the consequence if there were no messenger to explain the intermediary category?
A) People would be able to deduce duties on their own.
B) It would allow permission to abandon obligations and commit prohibitions.
C) Wisdom would be fully realized without messengers.
D) The intermediary category would not exist.

Key Takeaway
The necessity of prophets is rationally proven because without them, we would be unable to know obligatory and prohibited actions based on consequences, leading to a violation of divine wisdom.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The lesson shows that without a messenger, we would be permitted to abandon duties and commit sins. In what areas of your life have you relied on your own reasoning rather than the guidance of the prophets, possibly falling into that very permission? What specific step will you take today to seek prophetic guidance on a duty you have been neglecting?
?
If you truly believe that every action has a consequence tied to divine wisdom, how does that change your view of the obligations you find inconvenient? Are you willing to submit to the messenger's teachings even when you cannot see the immediate benefit? What will you do this week to align a specific area of your life with the revealed guidance?
?
The author argues that Allah has never left the world without a proof. How does this reality confront your tendency to make excuses for disobeying? Since the proof is available, what is stopping you from acting on it—and what would it cost you to ignore it?

The Three Categories of People
Author enumerates three categories of rational beings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author classifies people into three categories based on their intellectual capacities and worldly engagements.

Core Idea
People are divided into three types: the devoted intellectuals, the worldly-occupied, and the dull-minded.

Before arguing why people need prophets, the author first identifies three distinct groups among rational beings. Each group has a different relationship with intellect and worldly concerns. This classification sets the stage for understanding that not everyone can rely on reason alone.

Guided Path
1
Read the classification passage
Read the Arabic passage that describes the three categories. Notice how each group is defined by its qualities.
The first group is sharp and devoted to reflection; the second is sound but worldly; the third is dull and animalistic.
2
Identify each category in your own words
After reading, summarize each group in one sentence. This helps internalize the distinctions.
3
Reflect on the purpose of classification
Think about why the author starts with this classification. What does it set up for the later argument about the need for prophets?
This classification is the foundation for showing that most people need divine guidance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على أن الحاجة ماسة في قسمي الواجب والممتنع اللذين في العقول إمكان الوقوف عليهما في الجملة، إلى البيان الوارد عن الله تعالى لمعنيين: أحدهما يختص ببعض العقلاء. والآخر يشمل الجميع. فأما المعنى الخاص فهو ما مر في أول الكتاب في مسألة إيمان المقلد من انقسام الناس إلى أقسام ثلاثة. أحدهما الموصوفون بحدة الخواطر والأذهان ووفور العقل والألباب، المتفرغون للتأمل والتفكر في المباحث النظرية والمعالم الإلهية، المعرضون عن الذات البهيمية والمطالب الجسمانية. والثاني: الموسومون برجاحة العقول وقوة الخواطر المشتغلون بالمصالح الدنيوية والمكاسب التي بها تقوم أسباب المعيشة للخلق المعرضون عن تعاطي النظر والاستدلال والتأمل في الدلائل العقلية. والثالث: المجبولون على بلادة الأفهام وغلظ الخواطر الذين استولت عليهم الطبيعة البهيمية والنفس السبعية. ثم من المعلوم أن القسم الأول إن كان لهم بعقولهم الوافرة المتفرغة للبحث عن حقائق الأمور والمعالم النظرية مندوحة عن الرسل وغنية عن اتصال المواد الوحيية بهم فيما يحتاجون إليه في مصالح داريهم، فلا غنية بالقسمين الآخرين عن ذلك، لقصر الفريق الثاني عقولهم وأذهانهم على اكتساب العاجلة وصرفهم جل همهم وكدحهم على استجلاب اللذات الحاضرة، وتعذر وقوف الفريق الثالث بما لهم من العقول الناقصة والأفهام البليدة على ما يجب عليهم من حقوق خالقهم وشكر ما أثنائه يتقلبون في أحوالهم من أنواع النعم وصنوف اللذات التي درت في جميع عليهم من صانعهم، بل انسداد طريق ذلك عليهم لو تركوا مجرد عقولهم فلابد لهم من بيان ذلك ليتوصلوا إلى شكر خالقهم، وما استحق عليهم من العبادة. فكان إرسال الله الرسول إليهم إثباتًا لطريق معرفته، والوقوف على ما افترض عليهم من حقوقه، كالمعقول في حق الفريق الأول. ولا شك أن القسم الأول بالإضافة إلى القسمين الآخرين في حد القلة والندارة بل في حد الشذوذ والندرة، وما هذا سبيله لا عبرة به ولا اكتراث له بل العبرة للجم الغفير والخلق الكثير والله الموفق.
Indeed, the need is urgent in the two categories of the obligatory and the impossible—which the intellects can potentially grasp in general—for the statement coming from Allah the Exalted for two reasons: one specific to some rational beings, and the other encompassing all. As for the specific meaning, it is what was mentioned earlier in the book in the issue of the faith of the imitator (īmān al-muqallid) regarding the division of people into three categories. First: those described as sharpness of intellects and minds, abundance of reason and hearts, devoted to reflection and thought in theoretical investigations and divine realities, turning away from animalistic desires and bodily pursuits. Second: those distinguished by soundness of intellects and strength of minds, occupied with worldly interests and gains by which the means of livelihood for creation are established, turning away from engaging in rational investigation, deduction, and reflection on intellectual proofs. Third: those created with dullness of understanding and coarseness of minds, upon whom the animalistic nature and beastly soul have prevailed. Then it is known that the first category—even if they, with their abundant intellects devoted to seeking the realities of things and theoretical principles, have an alternative to the messengers and are independent of the connection of revelatory materials to them in what they need for the interests of their two abodes—still the other two categories are not independent of that. This is because the second group has limited their intellects and minds to acquiring the immediate and have turned their main concern and effort to attracting present pleasures; and the third group is prevented from knowing, with their deficient intellects and dull understandings, what is obligatory upon them of the rights of their Creator and gratitude for the blessings and kinds of pleasures that have flowed upon them from their Maker. Rather, the way to that is blocked for them if they were left to their mere intellects. So they must have a statement of that to arrive at gratitude to their Creator and what is due upon them of worship. Thus, Allah's sending a messenger to them is an establishment of the way to knowledge of Him and to knowing what He has obligated upon them of His rights, as is reasonable regarding the first group. There is no doubt that the first group, relative to the other two, is at the extreme of scarcity and rarity, indeed at the extreme of deviation and rareness; such a thing is not considered nor regarded; rather, consideration is for the great multitude and the many people. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of the 'specific reason' (al-maʿnā al-khāṣṣ) why people need divine guidance. The author divides humanity into three categories based on intellectual capacity and engagement with the world: (1) those with sharp minds devoted to theoretical and divine matters, (2) those with sound minds preoccupied with worldly gains, and (3) those with dull minds overcome by animalistic nature. He argues that the first category might, in theory, be independent of prophets due to their intellectual focus. However, the other two categories cannot attain knowledge of their duties and gratitude to their Creator through reason alone—the second is too busy with worldly pursuits, and the third has deficient intellect. Therefore, they need prophetic guidance. The author then emphasizes that the first category is extremely rare and insignificant compared to the majority, so the need for prophets is universal. The conclusion is that sending messengers is the means to establish knowledge of God and His rights.

Key Terms
الخواطر
الأذهان
العقول الناقصة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that all people are equally capable of rational reasoning about God.
Correction: The author shows that people vary greatly in intellectual capacity and engagement, so not everyone can reach divine truths through reason alone.

Checkpoint
Which category of people is described as 'occupied with worldly interests and gains, turning away from rational investigation'?
A) The first category
B) The second category
C) The third category
D) All categories

Key Takeaway
People are not uniform in intellect and focus; they fall into three broad categories that determine their ability to know God through reason alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of these three categories most accurately describes you right now? Are you spending your time and energy on deep intellectual pursuit of the divine, or are you consumed by worldly needs? What would a neutral observer conclude from your daily habits?
?
If you find yourself in the second category—sound intellect but distracted by life—what specific worldly pursuits are keeping you from engaging with the proofs of God? Will you set aside even 15 minutes today to ponder a rational proof?
?
The third category is dominated by animal nature. Do you see any part of yourself that acts purely from impulse or base desire, ignoring higher thought? What would it take for you to overcome that pull and choose the path of reflection? Make a concrete plan before you move on.

Why Most People Need Prophets
Author proves the necessity of prophets for the majority based on the classification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the second and third categories of people cannot fulfill their duties to God through reason alone, and why the first category is too rare to be the norm.

Core Idea
The majority of people—those preoccupied with world or dull-minded—cannot know God's rights without prophets.

Having classified people into three groups, the author now argues that the first group might theoretically be independent of prophets, but the other two absolutely need divine guidance. Moreover, the first group is extremely rare, so the need for prophets is universal. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument passage
Read the Arabic starting from 'ثم من المعلوم' to the end. Notice the logical steps.
The author first states a conditional, then explains the deficiency of the second and third groups.
2
Identify the reasoning for each group
Why can't the second group rely on reason? Why can't the third? Write down the reasons.
The second group is too busy with worldly pursuits; the third has deficient intellects.
3
Understand the role of the rare first group
The author says the first group is 'at the extreme of scarcity and rarity' so they are not considered. Why does this matter?
It shows that the need for prophets is not based on a small elite but on the vast majority.
4
Connect to the overall aim
Reflect on how this argument proves the necessity of prophethood for most people.

This passage is a detailed explanation of the 'specific reason' (al-maʿnā al-khāṣṣ) why people need divine guidance. The author divides humanity into three categories based on intellectual capacity and engagement with the world: (1) those with sharp minds devoted to theoretical and divine matters, (2) those with sound minds preoccupied with worldly gains, and (3) those with dull minds overcome by animalistic nature. He argues that the first category might, in theory, be independent of prophets due to their intellectual focus. However, the other two categories cannot attain knowledge of their duties and gratitude to their Creator through reason alone—the second is too busy with worldly pursuits, and the third has deficient intellect. Therefore, they need prophetic guidance. The author then emphasizes that the first category is extremely rare and insignificant compared to the majority, so the need for prophets is universal. The conclusion is that sending messengers is the means to establish knowledge of God and His rights.

Key Terms
الجم الغفير
الشذوذ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that intelligent people do not need prophets at all.
Correction: The author shows that even the first group's independence is only theoretical and conditional; in practice, they are extremely rare, and the majority definitely need prophets.

Checkpoint

C) They refuse to use reason
D) They are animalistic by nature

Key Takeaway
Most people cannot know God's rights through reason alone, so prophets are a necessity for the majority.

?

Three Categories of People and the Necessity of Prophets
Classifies people into three groups and argues the latter two need prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why most people, despite having intellect, require prophets to fulfill their duties to God.

Core Idea
Most people cannot fulfill their duties to God without prophetic guidance.

The author classifies humanity into three groups based on their intellectual capacity and worldly preoccupation. While a rare few may reach truth by intellect alone, the vast majority require revelation. This passage establishes the necessity of prophethood for the common person.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Try to grasp the three groups mentioned.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the three groups
Locate the descriptions of the second and third groups. Notice how the first group is described later in relation to the others.
The author does not list all three at once; he builds the argument.
3
Understand the argument for necessity
Focus on why the second and third groups need prophets. The first group is independent but extremely rare.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider that the first group is negligible; the general rule is that humanity needs prophets. This is a proof for prophethood.

Worldly matters and gains by which the means of livelihood are established for the creation who are averse to engaging in speculation, inference, and reflection upon rational proofs. And the third: those created with dullness of understanding and coarseness of minds, whom bestial nature and predatory soul have overpowered. Then it is known that the first category, if they have abundant intellects free for investigating the realities of things and theoretical principles, are independent of messengers and need not connect with revelatory materials regarding what they need for the interests of their two abodes, then the other two categories are not independent of that, because the second group's intellects and minds are limited to acquiring the immediate and they devote most of their concern and labor to obtaining present pleasures, and it is impossible for the third group, with their deficient intellects and dull understandings, to comprehend what is obligatory upon them of the rights of their Creator and gratitude for His favors? in which they are turning over in their states from types of blessings and kinds of pleasures that have flowed? upon them from their Maker; rather, the path to that is blocked for them if they are left with their bare intellects, so they must have an explanation of that to attain gratitude to their Creator and what worship is due from them. So God's sending the messenger to them is an establishment of the path to knowledge of Him and to understanding what He has imposed upon them of His rights, similar to what is rationally understood for the first group. And there is no doubt that the first category in relation to the other two categories is at the level of fewness and scarcity, rather at the level of rarity and paucity, and what is like this is not considered nor regarded; rather, consideration is for the great multitude and the many creation. And God is the granter of success.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage classifies people into three groups regarding their need for prophets. The author first describes the second group: those preoccupied with worldly gains and averse to rational speculation. Then the third group: those with dull intellects and coarse minds, dominated by animalistic and predatory instincts. He then argues that the first group—those with abundant, free intellects dedicated to investigating truth—may be independent of messengers and revelation. However, the other two groups cannot do without them. The second group's minds are limited to immediate acquisitions and pleasures, while the third group's deficient intellects cannot grasp their duties to God or gratitude for His blessings. Without revelation, the path to these duties is blocked. Therefore, God sends messengers to establish the knowledge of Him and His rights, just as reason supports the first group. The author concludes that the first group is extremely rare, so the general rule is that the majority of humanity—the countless multitude—needs prophets. This is a proof for the necessity of prophethood.

Intellect's Weakness and the Need for Revelation
Argues that creation implies weakness, so intellect needs revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Māturīdī tradition argues that human intellect, being created and inherently weak, requires divine revelation to attain true knowledge.

Core Idea
The intellect is created and weak; revelation is its necessary helper.

This lesson explores a foundational argument for the necessity of prophethood from the Māturīdī tradition. The author, Imām al-Nasafī, begins by establishing that the intellect, though a gift, is created and therefore subject to various defects and limitations. These weaknesses prevent it from reliably attaining the deepest truths on its own. Hence, a divine assistant—revelation—is indispensable. Let's examine the passage and unpack its reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage slowly. Notice how the author builds his case from the premise 'intellect is created' to the conclusion that revelation is needed.
Pay attention to the list of defects that afflict the intellect.
2
Identify the weaknesses of the intellect
List the specific defects mentioned: boredom, weariness, doubts, desires, lusts, worries, pains, etc. Why do these make the intellect insufficient for theoretical inquiry?
3
Connect to the necessity of revelation
Reflect on how the argument logically leads to the need for an external assistant. How does revelation help the intellect overcome its limitations and reach what must be reached?
The author concludes that this assistant is divine revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العقل مخلوق لذا يلحقه الضعف: وأما المعنى الشامل لجميع طبقات العقلاء وهو أن العقل شيء مخلوق، لابد من لحوق الآفات به وحلول الفترة والكلال به عند استيلاء الضجر والملال على صاحبه، وربما تعارضه الشبهات، وتصده عن حقيقة النظر الأماني والشهوات، وتمنعه عن الإحاطة بكل دقيق من الأمور وجليل، اعتراء الهموم وأسباب شغل القلب على صاحبه، وترادف الآلام والأوجاع عليه، وتشغله عن الاستقصاء في البحث والتأمل مع ما في المطالب النظرية من الغموض والدقة فلابد من معاون له إياه ليصل باتصاله به إلى ما يجب الوصول إليه. وذلك هو الوحي السماوي، والله الموفق.
The intellect is created, so weakness attaches to it. And as for the comprehensive meaning that encompasses all classes of rational beings: it is that the intellect is a created thing, inevitably defects attach to it, and languor and weariness settle upon it when boredom and tedium overpower its possessor. Perhaps doubts conflict with it, and desires and lusts turn it away from the reality of speculation, and prevent it from encompassing every subtle and great matter, the affliction of worries and causes of heart-occupation upon its possessor, and the succession of pains and ailments upon him, and distract him from thoroughness in investigation and reflection, given what is in theoretical inquiries of obscurity and subtlety. So he inevitably needs an assistant to help him, by whose connection he may reach what must be reached. That is divine revelation. And God is the granter of success.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the necessity of revelation based on the inherent weakness of human intellect. The author begins by stating a universal principle: the intellect is created (makhluq), and therefore weakness inevitably attaches to it. He then explains that this weakness manifests in various ways: defects, boredom, weariness, doubts, desires, and lusts that distract from true speculation. The intellect cannot encompass all matters, subtle or great, due to worries and physical ailments that preoccupy the mind. Given the obscurity and precision of theoretical inquiries, the intellect alone cannot attain truth. Therefore, it needs an external assistant, which is divine revelation (al-wahy al-samawi). This revelation helps the intellect reach what it must attain. The author concludes by invoking God's success. The argument is that since the intellect is created and thus deficient, it cannot suffice for the most important knowledge, making revelation indispensable.

Revelation Eases the Effort of the Intellect
Shows that revelation alleviates intellectual hardship even if intellect is capable.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that even if the intellect could independently attain all truths, revelation is still necessary because it spares the immense hardship of independent inquiry.

Core Idea
Revelation lightens the intellectual burden even for capable minds.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi presents a subtle argument for the necessity of prophethood. Even assuming the intellect could theoretically reach all truths, the effort required would be overwhelming. Revelation serves as a divine shortcut, alerting and guiding the intellect to make the pursuit of knowledge easy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully

Pay attention to the concessive tone; the author is not denying the intellect's capability but showing its practical limitation.
2
Identify the two scenarios
The author describes the hardship of unaided intellect (great difficulty, heavy burden) and then the ease when revelation guides it. Locate these contrasting descriptions.
3
Reflect on the implication

This connects to the broader theme of the necessity of prophets.

على أن العقول لو كان في جبلتها إمكان الوصول إلى جميع مصالح الدارين إلا أن ذلك لن يكون إلا بآداب الفكر، ونصّ مطية الخاطر، والانكباب على النظر الدائم والبحث الكامل، ويلحقه بذلك مشقة عظيمة، وتلزمه مؤنة كثيرة. ثم إنه إذا نبه على ذلك بالسمع وأرشد إلى كيفية استخراج ما يرومه بعقله تنبه لذلك، وسهل عليه الأمر وخفت له المؤنة.

Then, if one is alerted to that by revelation (al-sam‘) and guided to the method of extracting what he seeks by his intellect, he becomes alert to it, the matter becomes easy for him, and the burden becomes light.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage presents a further benefit of revelation: it reduces the immense difficulty of independent intellectual inquiry. The author concedes hypothetically that intellects might have the innate capacity to reach all truths concerning both this world and the next. However, even in that case, achieving such knowledge would require rigorous discipline of thought, intense mental exertion, constant speculation, and complete investigation—all accompanied by great hardship and heavy burden. Revelation (al-sam‘) provides a shortcut: it alerts the intellect and guides it to the method of extracting desired knowledge. When revelation points the way, the intellect is alerted, the task becomes easy, and the burden is lightened. Thus, revelation is beneficial not only for those who cannot reason independently but also for those who can, as it spares them enormous effort. The argument reinforces the utility and necessity of prophets.

Empirical Evidence: Revelation Guides the Simple
Points to the steadfastness of simple prophetic followers versus the error of philosophers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses the empirical observation of two groups—followers of prophets and philosophers—to demonstrate the necessity of revelation as a guide superior to intellect alone.

Core Idea
Revelation keeps simple people on truth; intellect alone often leads to error.

The author presents a striking empirical observation: the followers of prophets, despite being simple and unskilled in speculation, consistently adhere to truth, while philosophers, with their sharp intellects and dedicated study, frequently fall into error. This contrast points to a vital factor: revelation. Let us examine the passage to see how this argument unfolds.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the contrasting descriptions of the two groups.
The passage ends abruptly with 'لتأيد' (because… is supported). This introduces the reason.
2
Identify the two groups
Identify the followers of prophets and the philosophers. Note the characteristics attributed to each.
Followers: lacking speculation, dullness, busy with livelihood. Philosophers: sound intellect, strong minds, devoted years to study.
3
Observe the contrast in outcomes
See that followers persist in truth, while philosophers deviate into error and disbelief.
4
Understand the cause: revelation
The author states that the difference is because the first group is supported by revelation (māddat al-waḥy). This is the key point.
Revelation is the decisive factor that keeps people on truth, even without intellect.
5
Reflect on the implication
Think about what this means for the necessity of prophets and revelation. Why cannot intellect alone suffice?
This provides a practical proof for prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولهذا كان الغالب في اتباع الأنبياء عليهم السلام الاستمرار على الحق والتشبث به، وإن كان أكثرهم خالين عن صناعة النظر موصوفين بالبلادة، مشغولين باكتساب أسباب المعاش والغالب على الفلاسفة العدول عن الصواب والوقوع في الكفر والضلال، وإن كانوا موسومين برجاحة العقول وقوة الألباب وصفاء القرائح، متفرغين سنين كثيرة وأعمارًا طويلة للبحث عن المعالم الإلهية والمعاني الدينية، معتزلين الخلق في مدارسهم، لتأيد الصنف الأول بمادة الوحي
And for this reason the prevailing characteristic of the followers of the prophets, peace be upon them, is persistence upon the truth and adherence to it, even though most of them are devoid of the art of speculation, described with dullness, occupied with acquiring the means of livelihood. And the prevailing characteristic of the philosophers is deviation from correctness and falling into disbelief and misguidance, even though they are marked with soundness of intellects, strength of minds, and clarity of dispositions, devoting many years and long lifetimes to researching divine principles and religious meanings, isolating themselves from people in their schools, because the first group is supported by the substance of revelation.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage provides empirical evidence for the necessity of revelation by comparing two groups: followers of prophets and philosophers. The author observes that the followers of prophets generally persist in truth and adhere to it, despite most of them lacking the art of speculative reasoning and being characterized by dullness, busy with worldly livelihoods. In contrast, philosophers, who are known for their sound intellects, strong minds, and clear dispositions, and who devote many years and long lifetimes to researching divine matters in isolation, are more often found to deviate from correctness and fall into disbelief and misguidance. The reason for this difference, the author suggests, is that the first group (prophetic followers) is supported by the substance of revelation (māddat al-waḥy). This demonstrates that revelation is a crucial aid that keeps people on the truth, even without great intellectual capacity, whereas reliance on intellect alone, despite its strength, often leads to error. This is a practical proof for the necessity of prophets.

Key Terms
أنبياء (prophets)
فلاسفة (philosophers)
وحي (revelation)
عقل (intellect)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that intellectual superiority guarantees truth in religious matters.
Correction: The passage shows that philosophers, despite their intellect, often fall into error, while simple followers of prophets adhere to truth due to revelation.

Checkpoint
What empirical observation does the author cite to prove the effectiveness of revelation?
A) Philosophers always follow the truth
B) Followers of prophets often err despite intelligence
C) Simple followers of prophets remain on truth while philosophers often err
D) Both groups are equally correct

Key Takeaway
Revelation is a crucial support that keeps people on truth, even when intellect is lacking, and is therefore necessary for divine guidance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are faced with a difficult question about faith, do you instinctively turn to your own reasoning or to the guidance of revelation? Where has your intellect led you into confusion or doubt? Commit today to seeking answers first from the revealed sources before relying on your own mind.
?
The philosophers in this passage spent years searching for truth in isolation, yet they fell into error. In your own life, are there areas where you trust your education, intelligence, or research more than the clear teachings of the prophets? What would it take for you to humble yourself and accept revelation over your own conclusions?
?
The simple followers of the prophets, despite their dullness and worldly preoccupations, held firmly to the truth because of revelation. Do you sometimes look down on those with less knowledge or intellect, thinking you are better guided? Examine your heart: is your reliance on revelation as strong as theirs, or do you subtly pride yourself on your understanding?

Prophethood
intermediate
6 min
Empirical Evidence: Followers of Prophets vs Philosophers
Contrasts steadfastness of prophet followers with deviation of philosophers, proving revelation's benefit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the empirical observation of prophet followers' steadfastness versus philosophers' deviation proves that divine revelation, not human intellect, is the true guide to truth.

Core Idea
Revelation keeps the simple-minded on truth; intellect alone leaves the brilliant in error.

Imam al-Nasafi presents a powerful empirical argument: look at the followers of prophets—ordinary people, often dull and occupied with worldly tasks—yet they persist in truth and cling to it. Then look at the philosophers—brilliant, well-studied, and dedicated—yet they fall into kufr and misguidance. The only difference? Prophetic revelation. This lesson unpacks that contrast and its profound implication.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage (source_arabic) and its literal translation (source_translation). Notice the key contrast between the two groups.
Pay attention to the adjectives describing each group: bilādah vs. rajāḥat al-‘uqūl.
2
Identify the argument's structure
The passage makes a comparison: prophet followers persist in truth despite deficiencies, philosophers deviate despite strengths. Then it gives the reason: revelation vs. lack thereof. Finally, it draws a moral conclusion about gratitude.
3
Examine the empirical evidence
The author claims that almost no philosopher adhered to tawḥīd and the afterlife except those who took from prophets. This is presented as an observable fact. Ask yourself: is this a strong argument?
This is a historical observation, not a logical proof, but it serves as practical evidence.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage ends with a sharp rebuke: anyone who does not receive this blessing with gratitude is a hopeless fool. Consider the urgency of appreciating revelation.
This connects to the lesson's core idea: revelation is a gift.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاستمرار على الحق سمة متبعي الرسل ولهذا كان الغالب في اتباع الأنبياء عليهم السلام الاستمرار على الحق والتشبث به، وإن كان أكثرهم خالين عن صناعة النظر موصوفين بالبلادة، مشغولين باكتساب أسباب المعاش والغالب على الفلاسفة العدول عن الصواب والوقوع في الكفر والضلال، وإن كانوا موسومين برجاحة العقول وقوة الألباب وصفاء القرائح، متفرغين سنين كثيرة وأعمارًا طويلة للبحث عن المعالم الإلهية والمعاني الدينية، معتزلين الخلق في مدارسهم، لتأيد الصنف الأول بمادة الوحي السماوي وخلاء الصنف الثاني عن ذلك، بل لا نكاد نجد أحدًا من الأوائل المنتسبين إلى الفلسفة متمسكاً بالتوحيد مقراً بوظائف الأمر والنهي معترفا بالحشر والمعاد على ما هو الحق إلا إذا كان من أتباع الأنبياء عليهم السلام أخذ الدين منهم أو من أتباعهم، وإذا كان الأمر كذلك فمن لم يتلق هذه النعمة العظيمة بالشكر، واعتقد أن الإرشاد إلى ذلك تسهيل الأمر عليه وتخفيف المؤنة خارج عن الحكمة، فهو الأحمق الذي لا دواء لحمقه ولا حيلة لبرئه عما ابتلى به من داء جهله والله الهادي.
Persisting upon the truth is a characteristic of the followers of the messengers. For this reason, the prevalent [trait] among the followers of the prophets, peace be upon them, is persisting upon the truth and clinging to it, even though most of them are devoid of the art of reflection and described as dullness, occupied with acquiring the means of livelihood, while the prevalent [trait] among the philosophers is deviation from correctness and falling into disbelief and misguidance, even though they are characterized by soundness of intellects, strength of minds, and purity of innate dispositions, having devoted many years and long lifetimes to research into divine markers and religious meanings, secluded from people in their schools, because the first group is supported by the substance of divine revelation while the second group is devoid of that. Rather, we almost never find anyone among the early ones affiliated with philosophy adhering to tawḥīd, affirming the duties of command and prohibition, acknowledging the resurrection and the final return as is the truth, unless he was from the followers of the prophets, peace be upon them, having taken the religion from them or from their followers. And if the matter is so, then whoever does not receive this great blessing with gratitude, and believes that guidance to that which makes the matter easy for him and lightens the burden is outside of wisdom, is the fool whose folly has no cure and no stratagem for his recovery from the disease of ignorance with which he is afflicted. And Allah is the Guide.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage provides an empirical argument for the superiority of revelation. The author states that it is characteristic of prophet followers to persist in truth, despite often being simple-minded (bilādah) and occupied with worldly tasks. In contrast, philosophers, despite their intelligence, free time, and research, often deviate into error and disbelief. The reason is that the former are supported by revelation (māddat al-waḥy), while the latter lack it. The author then notes that any philosopher who did adhere to tawḥīd and the afterlife did so only by taking from the prophets. Consequently, to be ungrateful for this blessing is sheer foolishness. The argument moves from observable reality to a stark moral conclusion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Intellectual ability and dedicated research are sufficient to arrive at correct religious truth.
Correction: The author shows that even the most intelligent philosophers fell into error without revelation, while ordinary prophet followers remained steadfast. Revelation is essential.

Checkpoint
What is the main reason the author gives for why followers of prophets persist in truth while philosophers deviate?
A) Prophets are naturally more intelligent.
B) Philosophers are too busy with worldly matters.
C) Followers of prophets are supported by divine revelation.
D) Philosophers lack intellectual strength.

Key Takeaway
Divine revelation, not human intellect, is the decisive factor in attaining and persisting in religious truth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When has your own intellect led you away from truth, and how did revelation—through the Quran or sunnah—pull you back? What step can you take today to rely more on revelation than your reasoning in a specific matter?
?
If you were stripped of all Islamic knowledge and could only use your mind, would you arrive at tawḥīd and the afterlife as described in the Quran? What does your answer reveal about your dependence on Allah's guidance?
?
The author calls ingratitude for revelation 'foolishness beyond cure.' In what area of your life have you been ungrateful for the guidance Allah has sent, and what concrete act of gratitude can you perform today?
